<p><b>Muslims</b> are people who follow or practice <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Monotheistic" class="mw-redirect" title="Monotheistic">monotheistic</a> <a href="/wiki/Abrahamic_religions" title="Abrahamic religions">Abrahamic religion</a>. Muslims consider the <a href="/wiki/Quran" title="Quran">Quran</a>, their <a href="/wiki/Holy_book" class="mw-redirect" title="Holy book">holy book</a>, to be the verbatim word of <a href="/wiki/God_in_Islam" title="God in Islam">God</a> as revealed to the <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_in_Islam" title="Muhammad in Islam">Islamic</a> <a href="/wiki/Prophets_and_messengers_in_Islam" title="Prophets and messengers in Islam">prophet and messenger</a> <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">Muhammad</a>. The majority of Muslims also follow the teachings and practices of Muhammad (<i><a href="/wiki/Sunnah" title="Sunnah">sunnah</a></i>) as recorded in traditional accounts (<i><a href="/wiki/Hadith" title="Hadith">hadith</a></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> "Muslim" is an <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic word</a> meaning "submitter" (to God).<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The beliefs of Muslims include: that God (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">الله</span>&#8206; <i><a href="/wiki/All%C4%81h" class="mw-redirect" title="Allāh"><i lang="ar-Latn" title="American Library Association – Library of Congress transliteration">Allāh</i></a></i>) is eternal, transcendent and absolutely one (<i><a href="/wiki/Tawhid" title="Tawhid">tawhid</a></i>); that God is incomparable, self-sustaining and neither begets nor was begotten; that Islam is the complete and universal version of a primordial faith that has been revealed before through many prophets including <a href="/wiki/Abraham_in_Islam" title="Abraham in Islam">Abraham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ishmael_in_Islam" title="Ishmael in Islam">Ishmael</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isaac_in_Islam" title="Isaac in Islam">Isaac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moses_in_Islam" title="Moses in Islam">Moses</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jesus_in_Islam" title="Jesus in Islam">Jesus</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-People-of-the-Book_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-People-of-the-Book-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> that these previous messages and revelations have been partially changed or corrupted over time (<i><a href="/wiki/Tahrif" title="Tahrif">tahrif</a></i>)<sup id="cite_ref-Distorted_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Distorted-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> and that the Quran is the final unaltered revelation from God (Final Testament).<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Qualifier">Qualifier</span></h2>
<p>The religious practices of Muslims are enumerated in the <a href="/wiki/Five_Pillars_of_Islam" title="Five Pillars of Islam">Five Pillars of Islam</a>: the declaration of faith (<i><a href="/wiki/Shahadah" class="mw-redirect" title="Shahadah">shahadah</a></i>), daily prayers (<i><a href="/wiki/Salat" class="mw-redirect" title="Salat">salat</a></i>), fasting during the month of <a href="/wiki/Ramadan" title="Ramadan">Ramadan</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Sawm" class="mw-redirect" title="Sawm">sawm</a></i>), almsgiving (<i><a href="/wiki/Zakat" title="Zakat">zakat</a></i>), and the pilgrimage to <a href="/wiki/Mecca" title="Mecca">Mecca</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Hajj" title="Hajj">hajj</a></i>) at least once in a lifetime.<sup id="cite_ref-WSU_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSU-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CIA_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>To become a Muslim and to convert to Islam, it is essential to utter the <i><a href="/wiki/Shahada" title="Shahada">Shahada</a></i>, one of the <a href="/wiki/Five_Pillars_of_Islam" title="Five Pillars of Islam">Five Pillars of Islam</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_faith" title="Declaration of faith">declaration of faith</a> and trust that professes that there is <a href="/wiki/Tawhid" title="Tawhid">only one</a> <a href="/wiki/God_in_Islam" title="God in Islam">God</a> <i>(<a href="/wiki/Allah" title="Allah">Allah</a>)</i> and that <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">Muhammad</a> is God's messenger.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> It is a set statement normally recited in Arabic: <i>lā ʾilāha ʾillā-llāhu muḥammadun rasūlu-llāh</i> (<span lang="ar" dir="rtl" title="Arabic language text">لَا إِلٰهَ إِلَّا الله مُحَمَّدٌ رَسُولُ الله</span>)  "There is no god but Allah, (and) Muhammad is the messenger of God."<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni Islam</a>, the shahada has two parts: <i>la ilaha illa'llah</i> (there is no god but <a href="/wiki/Allah" title="Allah">God</a>), and <i>Muhammadun rasul Allah</i> (<a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">Muhammad</a> is the messenger of God),<sup id="cite_ref-LS_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LS-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> which are sometimes referred to as the first <i>shahada</i> and the second <i>shahada</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Cornell9_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cornell9-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The first statement of the shahada is also known as the <i><a href="/wiki/Tahlil" title="Tahlil">tahlīl</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">Shia Islam</a>, the shahada also has a third part, a phrase concerning <a href="/wiki/Ali" title="Ali">Ali</a>, the first <a href="/wiki/Imamah_(Shia_doctrine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Imamah (Shia doctrine)">Shia Imam</a> and the fourth <a href="/wiki/Rashidun" title="Rashidun">Rashid caliph</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni Islam</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl" title="Arabic language text">وعليٌ وليُّ الله</span> (<i lang="ar-Latn" title="DIN 31635 Arabic (Arabic language) transliteration">wa ʿalīyyun walīyyu-llāh</i>), which translates to "Ali is the <i><a href="/wiki/Wali" title="Wali">wali</a></i> of God".<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Lexicology">Lexicology</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Islam#Etymology_and_meaning" title="Islam">Islam §&#160;Etymology and meaning</a></div>
<p>The word <i>muslim</i> (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">مسلم</span>&#8206;, <small>IPA:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Arabic" title="Help:IPA/Arabic">[ˈmʊslɪm]</a></span>; <span class="nowrap"><small>English: </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="/ʌ/: &#39;u&#39; in &#39;cut&#39;">ʌ</span><span title="&#39;z&#39; in &#39;zoom&#39;">z</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span></span>/</a></span></span>, <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="/ʊ/: &#39;u&#39; in &#39;push&#39;">ʊ</span><span title="&#39;z&#39; in &#39;zoom&#39;">z</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span></span>/</a></span></span>, <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="/ʊ/: &#39;u&#39; in &#39;push&#39;">ʊ</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span></span>/</a></span></span> or <i>moslem</i> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="/ɒ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;body&#39;">ɒ</span><span title="&#39;z&#39; in &#39;zoom&#39;">z</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span></span>/</a></span></span>, <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="/ɒ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;body&#39;">ɒ</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span></span>/</a></span></span><sup id="cite_ref-muslim_pron_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-muslim_pron-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>) is the <a href="/wiki/Active_participle" class="mw-redirect" title="Active participle">active participle</a> of the same verb of which <i>islām</i> is a <a href="/wiki/Verbal_noun" title="Verbal noun">verbal noun</a>, based on the <a href="/wiki/Triliteral" class="mw-redirect" title="Triliteral">triliteral</a> <i><a href="/wiki/S-L-M" class="mw-redirect" title="S-L-M">S-L-M</a></i> "to be whole, intact".<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> A female adherent is a <i>muslima</i> (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">مسلمة</span>&#8206;) (also <a href="/wiki/Transliteration" title="Transliteration">transliterated</a> as "Muslimah"<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> ). The plural form in Arabic is <i>muslimūn</i> (<span lang="ar" dir="rtl" title="Arabic language text">مسلمون</span>) or <i>muslimīn</i> (<span lang="ar" dir="rtl" title="Arabic language text">مسلمين</span>), and its feminine equivalent is <i>muslimāt</i> (<span lang="ar" dir="rtl" title="Arabic language text">مسلمات</span>). 
</p><p>The ordinary word in English is "Muslim". The word <i>Mosalman</i> (<a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a>: <span lang="fa" dir="rtl">مسلمان</span>&#8206;, alternatively <i>Mussalman</i>) is a common equivalent for <i>Muslim</i> used in <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a>. Until at least the mid-1960s, many English-language writers used the term <i><a href="/wiki/Mohammedan" title="Mohammedan">Mohammedans</a></i> or <i>Mahometans</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Although such terms were not necessarily intended to be <a href="/wiki/Pejorative" title="Pejorative">pejorative</a>, Muslims argue that the terms are offensive because they allegedly imply that Muslims worship Muhammad rather than God.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Other obsolete terms include <i>Muslimite</i><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> and <i>Muslimist</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>Musulmán</b>/<b>Mosalmán</b> (<a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a>: <span lang="fa" dir="rtl">مسلمان</span>&#8206;) is a synonym for <i>Muslim</i> and is modified from <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>. It is the origin of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> word <i><i lang="es" title="Spanish language text">musulmán</i></i>, the (dated) <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> <i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Muselmann</i></i>, the French word <i>musulman</i>, the <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a> words <i><i lang="pl" title="Polish language text">muzułmanin</i></i> and <i><i lang="pl" title="Polish language text">muzułmański</i></i>, the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> word <i><i lang="pt" title="Portuguese language text">muçulmano</i></i>, the <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a> word <i><i lang="it" title="Italian language text">mussulmano</i></i> or <i><i lang="it" title="Italian language text">musulmano</i></i>, the <a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian</a> word <i>musulman</i> and the <a href="/wiki/Greek_Language" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek Language">Greek</a> word <span lang="el" title="Greek language text">μουσουλμάνος</span> (all used for a Muslim).<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> In English it was sometimes spelled <b>Mussulman</b> and has become <a href="/wiki/Archaism" title="Archaism">archaic</a> in usage.
</p><p>Apart from Persian, Spanish, Polish, Portuguese, Italian, and Greek, the term could be found, with obvious local differences, in <a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dari_(Persian_dialect)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dari (Persian dialect)">Dari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pashto_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Pashto language">Pashto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">Urdu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bengali_language" title="Bengali language">Bengali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marathi_language" title="Marathi language">Marathi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Punjabi_language" title="Punjabi language">Punjabi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kazakh_language" title="Kazakh language">Kazakh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uzbek_language" title="Uzbek language">Uzbek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyz_language" title="Kyrgyz language">Kyrgyz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_language" title="Azerbaijani language">Azeri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maltese_language" title="Maltese language">Maltese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_language" title="Bosnian language">Bosnian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">Bulgarian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Sanskrit language">Sanskrit</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Meaning">Meaning</span></h2>
<p>The Muslim philosopher <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Arabi" title="Ibn Arabi">Ibn Arabi</a> said:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047036">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>A Muslim is a person who has dedicated his worship exclusively to God...<i>Islam</i> means making one's religion and faith God's alone.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_prophets">Other prophets</span></h3>
<p>The Qur'an describes many prophets and messengers within Judaism and Christianity, and their respective followers, as Muslim: <a href="/wiki/Adam_(Bible)" class="mw-redirect" title="Adam (Bible)">Adam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Noah" title="Noah">Noah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abraham_in_Islam" title="Abraham in Islam">Abraham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ishmael_in_Islam" title="Ishmael in Islam">Ishmael</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jacob" title="Jacob">Jacob</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islamic_view_of_Moses" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamic view of Moses">Moses</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Islamic_view_of_Jesus" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamic view of Jesus">Jesus</a> and his <a href="/wiki/Apostles" title="Apostles">apostles</a> are all considered to be Muslims in the Qur'an. The Qur'an states that these men were Muslims because they submitted to God, preached His message and upheld His values, which included praying, charity, fasting and pilgrimage. Thus, in Surah 3:52 of the Qur'an, Jesus' disciples tell him, "We believe in God; and you be our witness that we are Muslims (<i>wa-shahad be anna muslimūn</i>)." In Muslim belief, before the Qur'an, God had given the <a href="/wiki/Tawrat" class="mw-redirect" title="Tawrat">Tawrat</a> (<a href="/wiki/Torah" title="Torah">Torah</a>) to Moses, the <a href="/wiki/Zabur" title="Zabur">Zabur</a> (<a href="/wiki/Psalms" title="Psalms">Psalms</a>) to <a href="/wiki/David" title="David">David</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Injil" class="mw-redirect" title="Injil">Injil</a> (<a href="/wiki/Gospel" title="Gospel">Gospel</a>) to Jesus, who are all considered important <a href="/wiki/Prophets_of_Islam" class="mw-redirect" title="Prophets of Islam">Muslim prophets</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:442px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Islam_percent_population_in_each_nation_World_Map_Muslim_data_by_Pew_Research.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Islam_percent_population_in_each_nation_World_Map_Muslim_data_by_Pew_Research.svg/440px-Islam_percent_population_in_each_nation_World_Map_Muslim_data_by_Pew_Research.svg.png" decoding="async" width="440" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Islam_percent_population_in_each_nation_World_Map_Muslim_data_by_Pew_Research.svg/660px-Islam_percent_population_in_each_nation_World_Map_Muslim_data_by_Pew_Research.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Islam_percent_population_in_each_nation_World_Map_Muslim_data_by_Pew_Research.svg/880px-Islam_percent_population_in_each_nation_World_Map_Muslim_data_by_Pew_Research.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="863" data-file-height="443" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Islam_percent_population_in_each_nation_World_Map_Muslim_data_by_Pew_Research.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>World Muslim population by percentage (2010 data<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Muslims&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> from <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a>)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Muslim_population_map_2009.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Muslim_population_map_2009.png/220px-Muslim_population_map_2009.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="109" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Muslim_population_map_2009.png/330px-Muslim_population_map_2009.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Muslim_population_map_2009.png/440px-Muslim_population_map_2009.png 2x" data-file-width="4296" data-file-height="2120" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Muslim_population_map_2009.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map of Muslim populations by absolute number, (<a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a>, 2009)</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Islam#Demographics" title="Islam">Islam §&#160;Demographics</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Muslim_population" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by Muslim population">List of countries by Muslim population</a></div>
<p>The most populous Muslim-majority country is Indonesia, home to 12.7% of the world's Muslims,<sup id="cite_ref-Distrib_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Distrib-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> followed by Pakistan (11.0%), Bangladesh (9.2%), and Egypt (4.9%).<sup id="cite_ref-Islam_by_country_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Islam_by_country-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> About 20% of the world's Muslims live in the Middle East and North Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-Distrib_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Distrib-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Sizable minorities are also found in <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_India" title="Islam in India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_China" title="Islam in China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Russia" title="Islam in Russia">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Ethiopia" title="Islam in Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_the_Americas" title="Islam in the Americas">the Americas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Australia" title="Islam in Australia">Australia</a> and parts of <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Europe" title="Islam in Europe">Europe</a>. The country with the highest proportion of self-described Muslims as a proportion of its total population is Morocco.<sup id="cite_ref-JDB_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JDB-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Converts and immigrant communities are found in almost every part of the world.
</p><p>Over 75–90% of Muslims are <a href="/wiki/Sunni" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni">Sunni</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Sunni_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sunni-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sunni_Islam_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sunni_Islam-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The second and third largest sects, <a href="/wiki/Shia" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia">Shia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya" title="Ahmadiyya">Ahmadiyya</a>, make up 10–20%,<sup id="cite_ref-Shia_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shia-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> and 1%<sup id="cite_ref-ahmadi_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ahmadi-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> respectively.
</p><p>With about 1.9 billion followers (2019), almost a quarter of <a href="/wiki/World_population" title="World population">earth's population</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Islam is the <a href="/wiki/Major_religious_groups" title="Major religious groups">second-largest</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Growth_of_religion" title="Growth of religion">fastest-growing religion in the world</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> due primarily to the young age and high <a href="/wiki/Fertility_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Fertility rate">fertility rate</a> of Muslims,<sup id="cite_ref-pew_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pew-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> with Muslim having a rate of (3.1) compared to the world average of (2.5). According to the same study, <a href="/wiki/Religious_conversion" title="Religious conversion">religious switching</a> has no impact on Muslim population, since the number of people who <a href="/wiki/Convert_to_Islam" class="mw-redirect" title="Convert to Islam">embrace Islam</a> and those who <a href="/wiki/Apostasy_in_Islam" title="Apostasy in Islam">leave Islam</a> are roughly equal.<sup id="cite_ref-pew_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pew-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A Pew Center study in 2016 found that Muslims have the highest number of adherents under the age of 15 (or 34% of the total Muslim population) of any major religion, while only 7% are aged 60+ (the smallest percentage of any major religion). According to the same study, Muslims have the highest <a href="/wiki/Fertility_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Fertility rate">fertility rates</a> (3.1) of any major religious group.<sup id="cite_ref-Pew2016_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pew2016-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The study also found that Muslims (tied with <a href="/wiki/Hindus" title="Hindus">Hindus</a>) have the lowest average levels of <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">education</a> with an average of 5.6 years of schooling, though both groups have made the largest gains in educational attainment in recent decades among major religions.<sup id="cite_ref-Pew2016_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pew2016-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> About 36% of all Muslims have no formal schooling,<sup id="cite_ref-Pew2016_61-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pew2016-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> and Muslims have the lowest average levels of <a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">higher education</a> of any major religious group, with only 8% having <a href="/wiki/Academic_degree" title="Academic degree">graduate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Post-graduate" class="mw-redirect" title="Post-graduate">post-graduate</a> degrees.<sup id="cite_ref-Pew2016_61-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pew2016-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Islamic_culture" title="Islamic culture">Islamic culture</a></div>
<p>Muslim culture or Islamic culture are terms used to describe the cultural practices common to Muslims and historically Islamic people. The early forms of <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> culture, from the <a href="/wiki/Rashidun_Caliphate" title="Rashidun Caliphate">Rashidun Caliphate</a> to early <a href="/wiki/Umayyad" class="mw-redirect" title="Umayyad">Umayyad</a> perioud, were predominantly <a href="/wiki/Arab" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab">Arab</a>, <a href="/wiki/Byzantine" class="mw-redirect" title="Byzantine">Byzantine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Persians" title="Persians">Persian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levantine</a>. With the rapid expansion of the <a href="/wiki/Caliphate" title="Caliphate">Islamic empires</a>, Muslim culture has influenced and assimilated much from the <a href="/wiki/Persian_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Persian culture">Persian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Egyptian culture">Egyptian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkic_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkic people">Turkic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mongol" class="mw-redirect" title="Mongol">Mongol</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Asian" class="mw-redirect" title="South Asian">South Asian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malay_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Malay people">Malay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somali_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Somali people">Somali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Berber_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Berber people">Berber</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesian</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Moro_people" title="Moro people">Moro</a> cultures.
</p>
